    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="3edf11a813c54816a3f0c72850ce12b6">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '646cbb69-b19c-4af8-a8c7-522f3f3575bc'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {

                     <p>Beijing Key Laboratory of Construction Tailorable Advanced Functional Materials and Green Applications, School of Materials Science and Engineering, Beijing Institute of Technology, Beijing, 100081 China</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Jin/Haibo">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Lu/Jun" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a7" data-db-target-for="a7" aria-controls="a7" aria-haspopup="true" id="a7_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Jun Lu<i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-mail_outline"></i></span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a7" aria-labelledby="a7_Ctrl" role="region" id="a7">

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d40903636" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Polyanionic sodium ion cathodes have attracted lots of concern because of their excellent structural stability. However, the low specific capacity is still a pressing issue hampering their practical application. In this work, a medium-entropy NASICON-structure cathode Na<sub>3.5</sub>V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (Me-NVMP) is proposed. The Me-NVMP achieves a highly reversible specific capacity of 165.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (1.8–4.4&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) at 0.1&nbsp;C via the stepwise redox reactions of Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup>-Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup>, V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup>-Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup>, and V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup>-Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup>. More impressively, the Me-NVMP yields super rate capability and cycling stability via the regulation of configuration entropy in NASICON. Specifically, the Me-NVMP cathode can preserve a capacity retention of 83.5% after 10,000 cycles at 100&nbsp;C (17&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Furthermore, excellent cycling performance even at the temperature of 0&nbsp;°C (capacity retention of 93.45% at 20&nbsp;C after 1000 cycles) is also demonstrated. In situ X-ray diffraction analysis reveals that the enhanced performance can be mainly attributed to the solid–solution-type Na<sup>+</sup> storage behavior in Me-NVMP. Moreover, issues such as Jahn-Teller distortion of Mn<sup>3+</sup> and irreversible structural change at high voltage (&gt;4.0&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) are effectively mitigated. This work inspires a new strategy to design high-performance polyanionic electrode materials.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202314019-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202314019-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have made a significant contribution to the development of modern society.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0001_R_d40903628e526" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Energy.">1</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0004_R_d40903628e526" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Adv. Energy Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the limited lithium resources are no longer fully suitable for sustainable development as energy consumption observably increases.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0004_R_d40903628e531" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Adv. Energy Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted considerable attention because of their abundant resources, low cost, and high safety.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0005_R_d40903628e536" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Nat. Rev. Mater.">5</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0006_R_d40903628e536" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Nat. Commun.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The difference in standard electrode potential between Li/Li<sup>+</sup> (−3.02&nbsp;V) and Na/Na<sup>+</sup>(−2.71&nbsp;V) intrinsically results in a lower energy density of SIBs compared to LIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0007_R_d40903628e546" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Energy Stor. Mater.">7</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0009_R_d40903628e546" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Hence, there is an imperative requirement to develop cathode materials with high operation voltage and specific capacity for the rapid development and great practical utilization potential of SIBs.</p>
         
         <p>Up to now, a variety of cathode materials have been developed, containing transition metal layer oxides Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>MO<sub>2</sub> (M = Ni, Fe, Co, Mn, etc.),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0010_R_d40903628e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0014_R_d40903628e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Adv. Energy Mater.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Prussian blue analogs (PBAs) Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>P[R(CN)<sub>6</sub>] (P = Ni, Mn, Fe, Co, Cu; R = Co, Mn, Fe, etc.)<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0015_R_d40903628e570" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Chem">15</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0017_R_d40903628e570" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Mater.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and polyanionic compounds Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>M<sub>2</sub>(XO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (M = Ti, Mn, V, Fe, etc.; X = P, Si, S).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0018_R_d40903628e585" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Electrochem. Commun.">18</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0022_R_d40903628e585" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Structural defects caused by irreversible phase change and oxygen release together with the issue of air stability have greatly slowed down the commercialization process of the layer transition metal oxides in SIBs. Owing to the crystalline water from the preparation process and the high toxicity of cyanide, the Prussian blue compounds also require further efforts to meet the practical application requirements.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0023_R_d40903628e590" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J Mater Chem">23</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0024_R_d40903628e590" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the Na superionic conductor (NASICON)-structure polyanionic compounds have drawn extensive interest on account of their stable 3D framework structure facilitating the Na<sup>+</sup> migration. Well-documented Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> with a typical NASICON structure renders favorable electrochemical properties and can offer a reversible specific capacity of 117 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and an operational plateau of 3.4&nbsp;V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na associated with the redox couple of V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0025_R_d40903628e615" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Adv. Energy Mater.">25</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0026_R_d40903628e615" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Mater.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the high cost and toxicity of V element limits the widespread application of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> in large-scale energy storage devices.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0027_R_d40903628e629" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - J Mater Chem">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Meanwhile, the multivalent properties of the V are not adequately exploited and utilized, which further reduces the economic advantages of the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as a sodium ion cathode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0007_R_d40903628e643" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Energy Stor. Mater.">7</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0025_R_d40903628e643" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Adv. Energy Mater.">25</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0027_R_d40903628e643" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - J Mater Chem">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>It is possible to develop new NASICON-type phosphates by using relatively inexpensive and nontoxic metallic elements to replace V<sup>3+</sup> partially for the purpose of regulating the operating potential and then promoting the energy density.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0007_R_d40903628e652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Energy Stor. Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Cheaper transition metals such as Ti, Fe, and Mn seem to be promising alternatives to V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0028_R_d40903628e657" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Energy Mater.">28</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0032_R_d40903628e657" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the case of the Na<sub>4</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (2.5-3.8&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) cathode, the introduction of Mn can offer an additional high-voltage platform of Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> (3.6&nbsp;V), considerably increasing the average operation voltage of the cathode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0028_R_d40903628e676" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Energy Mater.">28</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0030_R_d40903628e676" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv. Energy Mater.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Although Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> shows great advantages as a sodium ion cathode in terms of working voltage and corresponding energy density, some unfavorable issues such as the Jahn-Teller effect correlated with Mn<sup>3+</sup>, seriously irreversible structural change within the high voltage region (&gt;4.0&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) need to be well addressed. If the redox reactions of V<sup>4+</sup>/<sup>5+</sup> (4.0&nbsp;V) and Mn<sup>3+</sup>/<sup>4+</sup> (4.1&nbsp;V) couples can be reversibly stimulated in the Na<sub>4</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode together with the superiority of structural stability, the energy density could reach a new height.</p>
         
         <p>Previous work has demonstrated that an increase in entropy can lead to more combinations of possible interactions, ultimately stabilizing the crystal structure and significantly improving the performance of the electrode materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0008_R_d40903628e710" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0009_R_d40903628e710" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Zhu et al. studied the electrochemical performance of Na<sub>3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>V<sub>2/3</sub>Ti<sub>2/3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C@CNTs (ME-NMVTP) between 1.5 and 4.3&nbsp;V, a reversible capacity of 158.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> was achieved at 20&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> with a long-term lifespan of 1000 cycles at 500&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>&nbsp;(capacity retention of 88.3%).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0033_R_d40903628e735" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Adv. Energy Mater.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Li et&nbsp;al. synthesized Na<sub>3.4</sub>Fe<sub>0.4</sub>Mn<sub>0.4</sub>V<sub>0.4</sub>Cr<sub>0.4</sub>Ti<sub>0.4</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, which showed a remarkably high capacity of 161.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (1.5-4.5&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na). However, the redox reaction of Cr<sup>4+</sup>/Cr<sup>3+</sup> is not stimulated and does not offer a capacity contribution.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0034_R_d40903628e766" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Sci.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Considering the above factors, in this work, we have developed a medium-entropy NASICON-type Na<sub>3.5</sub>V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (Me-NVMP) cathode based on structural stability and capacity improvement, which shows high-energy-density Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance with fast-charging property via combining the advantages of V, Mn, Fe and Ti electrochemical active elements as illustrated in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0001">1</a>. The highly reversible redox reactions (1.8–4.4&nbsp;V) of Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup>, Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup>, V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup> and Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup> couples are realized and the structural degradation induced by MnO<sub>6</sub> Jahn-Teller distortion and irreversible structural change above 4.0&nbsp;V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na is effectively mitigated. To be specific, compared with Na<sub>4</sub>VFe(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVFP) and Na<sub>2</sub>VTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVTP), the sodium ion storage capability of the Me-NVMP cathode is significantly enhanced. The charge compensation mechanism and structural evolution of the Me-NVMP during Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction were analyzed by ex situ X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) and In situ X-ray diffraction (XRD), respectively. This work provides a new approach to the design of multi-electron transfer and fast-charging cathodes for high-performance SIBs.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314019-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/38049ba9-a033-4e92-b9c2-13f2576d2581/adfm202314019-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/38049ba9-a033-4e92-b9c2-13f2576d2581/adfm202314019-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/caaf5c88-c5dc-4d8c-9e68-f4076ec1ef7e/adfm202314019-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/38049ba9-a033-4e92-b9c2-13f2576d2581/adfm202314019-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">

                  </div>

               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202314019-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202314019-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>Rietveld refinement analysis of X-ray diffraction (XRD) results was conducted to study the crystal structure and the purity of the sample. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0002">2a</a> presents the Rietveld refinement results for the medium-entropy compound Na<sub>3.5</sub>V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (Me-NVMP), and detailed information on the atomic positions is summarized in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information). The Rietveld refinement results converge to <i>R</i><sub>wp</sub> = 5.12% and <i>R</i><sub>p</sub> = 4.17% based on the X-ray diffraction data, with reasonable displacement and site occupation factors for all kinds of atoms. Moreover, the Me-NVMP exhibits a single pure phase consistent with the typical rhombohedral NASICON structure of the <i>R</i>-3c space group, and no impurity phase can be found. As illustrated in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information), both Na<sub>4</sub>VFe(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVFP) and Na<sub>2</sub>VTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVTP) possess high crystallinity and all diffraction peaks also correspond well to Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> phase (PDF No:97-024-8140). The relevant crystallographic information, atomic coordinates, and occupancy information are provided in Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information). It knows that the alloys can be classified into low entropy (Δ<i>S</i><sub>conf</sub> ≤ 0.69 R), medium entropy (0.69 R&lt;Δ<i>S</i><sub>conf</sub> &lt; 1.5 R), and high entropy (ΔS<sub>conf</sub> ≥ 1.5 R) categories according to the definition of statistical thermodynamics (Equations <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0035_R_d40903628e947" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Small Methods">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As illustrated in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information), the Me-NVMP with a configuration entropy of 1.38 R belongs to the category of medium entropy. The control groups, the NVFP and NVTP, are both low entropy of 0.69 R. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0002">2b</a> exhibits the schematic diagram of the Me-NVMP structure. As shown, it demonstrates a robust 3D framework structure consisting of the TMO<sub>6</sub> octahedra and PO<sub>4</sub> tetrahedra sharing the connection of O atom, with V, Mn, Fe, and Ti atoms sharing the octahedral position of 12c in the NASICON matrix. Wyckoff position of the Na<sub>1</sub> ion is 6b, with a six-site oxygen environment, while that of Na<sub>2</sub> ion is 18e, with an eight-site oxygen environment. Na<sub>2</sub> is more prone to participate in electrochemical reaction processes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0008_R_d40903628e969" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0034_R_d40903628e969" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Sci.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> 3.5Na per formula in the Me-NVMP cathode means that there is a higher concentration of removable Na<sup>+</sup>, suggesting that a more specific capacity can be released in the first cycle. The morphology and crystallography of Me-NVMP were researched by transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and scanning electron microscopy (SEM). As exhibited in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0002">2c</a>, the Me-NVMP presents irregular polyhedral-shaped particle sizes ranging from 750&nbsp;nm to 2.75&nbsp;µm. The NVFP and NVTP synthesized via the same method also present similar morphology and particle size distribution (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0002">2d</a> exhibits a clear depiction of the crystalline Me-NVMP and an amorphous carbon coating layer. High-resolution TEM (HRTEM) image of Me-NVMP indicates clear lattice stripes with a spacing of 0.45&nbsp;nm, corresponding to the (104) plane of the NASICON structure. The thickness of the carbon layer is about 2.9&nbsp;nm, which can observably enhance the electrical conductivity of the NASICON matrix and thus boost the reaction kinetic. The carbon content of 6.3% is determined by thermogravimetry analysis (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). In the selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0002">2e</a>), the lattice planes corresponding to (110), (116), and (006) are distinctly visible. The elemental ratio was identified by energy dispersive spectrometer (EDS) analysis and inductively coupled plasma-optical emission spectroscopy (ICP) analysis; the result is highly consistent with the initially designed composition (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information). High-angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (HAADF-STEM) image and the corresponding energy dispersive spectrometer (EDS) mapping (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0002">2f</a>) display a uniform distribution of V, Mn, Ti, and Fe elements throughout the Me-NVMP at a given resolution. In the meantime, these four kinds of metal elements can be clearly indicated in the XPS spectra, which can be taken as solid evidence of the successful co-substitution of these metal elements into the NASICON matrix (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314019-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3ac7e524-8448-4b11-bbfb-b1c7c46bd014/adfm202314019-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/3ac7e524-8448-4b11-bbfb-b1c7c46bd014/adfm202314019-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/58637aed-e5ae-487e-853c-c2030a05a5aa/adfm202314019-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3ac7e524-8448-4b11-bbfb-b1c7c46bd014/adfm202314019-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314019-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314019" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD pattern and Rietveld refinement result of the Me-NVMP. b) Schematic representation of the Me-NVMP crystal structure. c) SEM image (the inset is the particle size distribution curve of as-prepared Me-NVMP). d) High-resolution TEM image. e) Selected area electron diffraction pattern. f) HAADF STEM image and corresponding EDS mapping results for Me-NVMP.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In order to evaluate the electrochemical behavior of these cathodes, three kinds of electrodes were assembled in CR2032 coin cells with metallic Na as the anode and the reference electrode. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3a–f</a> displays the initial four charge/discharge profiles at 0.1&nbsp;C and cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves at 0.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> between 1.8 and 4.4&nbsp;V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na). Both NVFP and NVTP electrodes exhibit two distinct voltage plateaus corresponding to the redox couples of V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup> (≈3.4&nbsp;V) and Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> (≈2.4&nbsp;V) or Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup> (≈2.1&nbsp;V), respectively. However, the Me-NVMP electrode presents two extended plateaus from 2 to 2.5&nbsp;V and 3.3 to 3.6&nbsp;V, which can be ascribed to the combination of Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup>, Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> and V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup>, Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> redox pairs, respectively. Furthermore, it can be found that the access of the V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup> couple in the NVFP (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3e</a>) can be achieved in the first cycle. Nevertheless, the capacity contribution of the V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup> couple basically disappears after the second cycle (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3b</a>). This may be attributed to the fact that when the NVFP cathode is cycled above 4&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, the occupation of the Na1 site is not the thermodynamically stable and unrecovered local environment of vanadium atoms, resulting in severe structural deterioration accompanied by the loss of the high-voltage capacity during cycling.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0007_R_d40903628e1082" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Energy Stor. Mater.">7</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0008_R_d40903628e1082" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0037_R_d40903628e1082" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Energy Stor Mater.">37</a>-<a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0040_R_d40903628e1082" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Energy Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the charge/discharge curves and CV curves (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3a,d</a>) reveal that the Me-NVMP also renders an extended plateau at the high voltage region of 4.0–4.15&nbsp;V, which should be assigned to the stimulation of V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup> and Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup> couples, leading to a considerable increase in the energy density in comparison with the other electrodes. As a result, a specific discharge capacity of 165.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (1.8-4.4&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) at 0.1 C can be delivered (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3a</a>), exceeding most NASICON-structure sodium ion cathodes and layered oxide cathode materials (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information), and further affirming the full activation of the redox reactions of electrochemically active elements in the Me-NVMP. Furthermore, we found that the three voltage plateaus in the charge/discharge curve of Me-NVMP were obviously smoothed without affecting the discharge capacity, showing the characteristic slope curve of solid solution reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0036_R_d40903628e1113" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Sci. Adv.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast to the Na<sub>4</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, which exhibits rapid capacity decay at above 4.0&nbsp;V because of the severe structural irreversibility, the Me-NVMP can maintain excellent reversibility even at a voltage &gt;4.0&nbsp;V. It means that the strategy of integration/synergistic effects of medium entropy structure can prevent irreversible structural transformation and capacity decay at high voltage, and boost the electrochemical performance.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314019-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/913ea184-c900-4ce5-aace-872f87d16a30/adfm202314019-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/913ea184-c900-4ce5-aace-872f87d16a30/adfm202314019-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/aaf09682-2f38-4c41-8955-0267a5fa77af/adfm202314019-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/913ea184-c900-4ce5-aace-872f87d16a30/adfm202314019-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314019-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314019" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical properties of Me-NVMP (1&nbsp;C&nbsp;=&nbsp;171&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), NVFP (1&nbsp;C&nbsp;=&nbsp;110&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and NVTP (1&nbsp;C&nbsp;=&nbsp;124&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) cathodes evaluated in coin-type half-cells. The charge/discharge profiles at 0.1&nbsp;C and C–V curves at 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> of a,d) Me-NVMP, b,e) NVFP, and c,f) NVTP electrodes. g–i) Rate performance of three kinds of cathode and j–l) corresponding GCD curves at different current densities. m) Long-term cycling performance of Me-NVMP at 100&nbsp;C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Rate performance is also important for practical application. In distinct contrast to the NVFP (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3h</a>) and NVTP (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3i</a>), the Me-NVMP electrode renders outstanding rate performance. At the current densities of 0.1, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10, 20, 50, and 100 C, the Me-NVMP electrode can deliver specific capacities of 165.8, 159, 157, 150, 144, 132, 121, 98, and 69 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3g</a>). A capacity of 162 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> is well maintained when the rate is restored to 0.1 C, which surpasses the NVFP (≈100 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and NVTP (≈122 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>), suggesting a superior rate capability. Corresponding GCD curves of three kinds of electrodes at different rates are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3j–l</a>. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3j</a> shows that at 10 C the Me-NVMP can still exhibit a capacity platform at the high voltage &gt;4.0&nbsp;V, signifying a suppressed electrochemical polarization.</p>
         
         <p>Cycling stability was examined at different rates of 10, 20, 50, and 100 C. In general, the Me-NVMP exhibits excellent rate capability. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a> (Supporting Information) summarizes the long-term cycling performance of the Me-NVMP, NVFP, and NVTP electrodes at 10 C, it can be found that after 500 cycles the Me-NVMP has a much higher capacity retention than that of the NVTP and NVFP (97.2%&gt;88.6%&gt;80.7%). After 500 cycles at 10 C three pairs of voltage platforms at 2.25/2.21, 3.46/3.41 and 4.07/4.04&nbsp;V can be still observed in the d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> plot (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information); these redox peaks correspond to the couples of Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup>-Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup>, V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup>-Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup>, and V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup>-Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup>, respectively. The small potential gap of each redox pair suggests a highly reversible Na<sup>+</sup> storage process. In addition to the reduced relative intensity of these X-ray diffraction patterns, the Me-NVMP electrode can still preserve its pristine crystal structure after 500 cycles at 10 C, affirming the desirable stability of NASICON framework (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information). The high agreement of the charge transport kinetics is reconfirmed by comparing the initial and post-cycle EIS spectra of the Me-NVMP electrode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). Furthermore, The Me-NVMP can maintain the specific capacities of 153 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (99.2% of the initial capacity) after 100 cycles at 1 C, and 124 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (92.1% of the initial capacity) and 103 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (91.5% of the initial capacity) after 1000 cycles at 20 and 50 C, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information). More impressively, the Me-NVMP can preserve a discharge capacity of ≈69 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a retention of 83.5% after 10&nbsp;000 cycles at 100 C (≈17 A g<sup>−1</sup>) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0003">3m</a>). The capacity retentions for these electrodes are collected in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a> (Supporting Information). As illustrated, a well-designed Me-NVMP cathode for SIBs holds great potential to meet the practical demands for fast charging scenarios.</p>
         
         <p>The sodium storage mechanism of the Me-NVMP was characterized using In situ XRD analysis. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0004">4a</a> shows the characteristic diffraction peaks of the Me-NVMP at different charge/discharge stages and the corresponding 2D contour plots. Examining the patterns in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0004">4a</a> closely, the diffraction peaks of (104), (113), (116), and (300) continuously move toward high angle direction upon the charge process, which is ascribed to a contraction of the unit cell upon Na<sup>+</sup> extraction. In the subsequent discharge process, these diffraction peaks can go back to the pristine location, signifying a solid-solution-type of sodium ion storage behavior.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0036_R_d40903628e1263" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Sci. Adv.">36</a>, <a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0037_R_d40903628e1263" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Energy Stor Mater.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As is known, the solid solution mechanism implies a reduced migration barrier for Na<sup>+</sup> in comparison with the bi-phasic reaction mechanism and increases the kinetic reaction rate due to the fact that it does not involve the ordering rearrangement of sodium ions and vacancies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0036_R_d40903628e1271" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Sci. Adv.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, it is worth noting that the (211) diffraction peak periodically appears and disappears in the region of 3.8–4.4&nbsp;V, illustrating a bi-phasic storage mechanism for sodium ions. In conclusion, the main sodium storage mechanism for Me-NVMP is a solid–solution reaction coexisting with the bi-phasic reaction.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314019-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3dc656d0-0d26-40b6-af10-95ae6d663385/adfm202314019-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/3dc656d0-0d26-40b6-af10-95ae6d663385/adfm202314019-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/3e8f5925-4fe0-4e1f-88c1-443bfc1f6afd/adfm202314019-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3dc656d0-0d26-40b6-af10-95ae6d663385/adfm202314019-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314019-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314019" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The XRD patterns at different electrochemical stages and the corresponding 2D contour plot of the Me-NVMP. b) XPS spectra of the V 2p <sub>3/2</sub>, Mn 2p <sub>3/2</sub>, Fe 2p <sub>3/2</sub>, Ti 2p <sub>3/2</sub> that collected from the OCV, charged to 2.9&nbsp;V, charged to 3.7&nbsp;V, charged to 4.4&nbsp;V, discharged to 1.8&nbsp;V of the Me-NVMP. c) Volumetric variation for the Me-NVMP and other typical sodium/lithium-ion cathode materials.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information) displays the detailed changes in the lattice parameters of Me-NVMP at selected electrochemical states. Upon charging to 4.4&nbsp;V, the lattice constant <i>a</i> changes from 8.8051 to 8.6748 Å and <i>c</i> varies from 21.7258 to 21.6547 Å, which is attributed to a decrease in Na<sup>+</sup> occupancy and the radius of transition metal ions. During the subsequent discharge process, the lattice parameters <i>a</i> and <i>c</i> get increased again. This indicates that the lattice constants of the Me-NVMP change reversibly during the electrochemical process. In addition, the volume change of the Me-NVMP is calculated to be 3.8%, which is much lower than most well-documented sodium ion cathodes, implying that the Me-NVMP undergoes a low-strain operation during the charge/discharge process and verifying the feasibility of enhancing structural stability via rationally regulating the configuration entropy (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0004">4c</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0008_R_d40903628e1324" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the corresponding Na<sup>+</sup> extraction/insertion process in Me-NVMP is demonstrated in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a> (Supporting Information). The original Me-NVMP containing 3.5Na per mol, was initially charged to achieve a Na-deficient phase NaV<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>. The fully discharged Na-rich phase is identified to be Na<sub>4</sub>V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>.</p>
         
         <p>In addition, the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was used to evaluate the capability of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion. The GITT curves and calculated <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of the Me-NVMP cathode during the second cycle are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a> (Supporting Information). The Me-NVMP shows small fluctuations in <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> values in a relatively narrow range of about 10<sup>−9</sup>-10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup> upon cycling at room temperature. Specifically speaking, the decline in <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> can be observed within the regions of three redox plateaus, implying slow dynamic processes. As is well known, high pseudo-capacitance contribution is crucial for the rate performance of the electrode materials. In order to evaluate the pseudo-capacitance contribution of Me-NVMP, CV analysis was conducted at different scan rates (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a</a>, Supporting Information). In the range of 0.1-1 mVs<sup>−1</sup>, the <i>b</i>-values of Me-NVMP can be identified as 0.982, 0.745, and 0.779 for the oxidation peaks and 0.954, 0.871, and 0.794 for the reduction peaks (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18b</a>, Supporting Information), indicating that the kinetics of sodium ion storage is mainly pseudo-capacitive behavior. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18c</a> (Supporting Information) shows the proportion of pseudo-capacitance contribution at 0.8&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, where the percentage contribution is as high as 91.75%. The proportional of pseudo-capacitance contribution in total gets increased from 80.79% (0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>) to 93.02% (1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18d</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>The XPS spectra of V, Mn, Fe, and Ti elements at open circuit voltage (OCV), charge to 2.9&nbsp;V, charge to 3.7&nbsp;V, charge to 4.4&nbsp;V, and discharge to 1.8&nbsp;V of the Me-NVMP were analyzed by ex situ XPS analysis to determine the role of each electrochemically active species in the process of multi-sodium ions storage reaction (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0004">4b</a>). At OCV, the V 2p <sub>3/2</sub> and Mn 2p <sub>3/2</sub> peaks are located at 516&nbsp;eV and 640.4&nbsp;eV, respectively, which are correlated with V<sup>3+</sup> and Mn<sup>2+</sup>. Then after charge to 3.7&nbsp;V, the V 2p <sub>3/2</sub> and Mn 2p <sub>3/2</sub> are found to move toward higher binding energy and the characteristic peak of V<sup>4+</sup> (516.5&nbsp;eV) and Mn<sup>3+</sup> (641.3&nbsp;eV) can be observed. When fully charged to 4.4&nbsp;V, the mixed states of V<sup>4+</sup>(516.5&nbsp;eV)/V<sup>5+</sup> (517.2&nbsp;eV) and Mn<sup>3+</sup>(641.3&nbsp;eV)/Mn<sup>4+</sup> (644&nbsp;eV) can be distinctly identified. As for Fe 2p <sub>3/2</sub> and Ti 2p <sub>3/2</sub>, the characteristic peaks of Fe<sup>2+</sup> (710.5&nbsp;eV) /Fe<sup>3+</sup> (715.4&nbsp;eV) and Ti<sup>3+</sup>(458.6&nbsp;eV) /Ti<sup>4+</sup> (462.5&nbsp;eV) can be determined in the pristine electrode. The relative intensity of Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> decreases while the relative intensity of Fe<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup> increases significantly during the charge process. Meanwhile, Fe<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup> can be found recovering back to Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> when being fully discharged to 1.8&nbsp;V, indicating that the redox reactions of Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> and Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup> are completely activated during the electrochemical process. The XPS results certify the multi-redox reactions of active elements in the Me-NVMP, which is well consistent with the voltage platforms in the charge/discharge curves (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0002">2a</a>).</p>
         
         <p>In addition, the electrochemical performance of the Me-NVMP cathode at low temperatures was investigated in order to indicate the application prospects of sodium-ion batteries in all-climate environments. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0005">5a–c</a> presents the EIS spectra of the Me-NVMP, NVTP, and NVFP cathodes at different temperatures, respectively. The results indicate that the Me-NVMP has a much lower diffusion activation energy than NVTP and NVFP (1.61 eV&lt;1.64&nbsp;eV &lt;1.78&nbsp;eV), indicating the desirable temperature-insensitive charge transport kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314019-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314019-bib-0037_R_d40903628e1500" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Energy Stor Mater.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0005">5d</a> shows the initial four charge/discharge profiles at 0.1 C and 0&nbsp;°C in the region of 1.8–4.4&nbsp;V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) for the Me-NVMP electrode, which can still display well-defined multiple charge/discharge plateaus. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0005">5e</a> illustrates the rate performance of the Me-NVMP cathode at 0&nbsp;°C. The Me-NVMP can deliver the specific capacities of 158, 151, 144, 132, 123, and 106 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1, 1, 2, 5, 10, and 20 C, respectively. The capacity can gradually recover to 155 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> as the rate gets back to 0.1 C. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0005">5f</a> presents the corresponding GCD curves at a different rate and it can be seen that the specific capacity at 0 °C and low rates such as 1 C, 2 C is still close to the specific capacity at room temperature. Furthermore, Me-NVMP at the low temperature of 0&nbsp;°C can deliver the specific capacity of 146 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (96.57% of the initial capacity)/135 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (95.43% of the initial capacity)/123 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (90.3% of the initial capacity) after 100/300/500 cycles at 2/5/10 C, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information). More importantly, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0005">5g</a> reveals that the Me-NVMP cathode can keep a capacity retention of 93.45% at a high rate of 20 C after 500 cycles. In addition, the electrochemical performance of the Me-NVMP cathode at −20 °C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information) is also excellent, further certifying its application prospects in low-temperature environments. We believe that with the optimization of the liquid electrolyte and the electrode-electrolyte interface, this medium-entropy electrode material will be able to shine in all-climate applications. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0005">5h</a> displays the GCD curves of Me-NVMP at 20 C and 0 °C. No noticeable variation can be identified over these curves, implying minimal capacity decay. The outstanding performance of Me-NVMP toward sodium ion storage in half-cells encourages us to further explore its performance in full cells. As illustrated in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0006">6a</a>, hard carbon (HC) was selected as the anode material for assembling the full cells. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a> (Supporting Information) provides the GCD curves and cycling performance of the HC anode. The HC anode can deliver a capacity of 260 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> and reveal a capacity retention of 85% after 100 cycles. The initial charge-discharge curves of the Me-NVMP//HC full cell at 0.1 C in the potential region of 1.5-4.1&nbsp;V are provided in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0006">6b</a>, which can offer a reversible specific capacity of 162&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> (based on the mass of cathode). The three extended platforms at 2-2.4, 3.3-3.4, and 3.9–4.0&nbsp;V can be clearly observed. In addition, the full cell can deliver high capacities of 161, 152, 145, 140, and 136 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, 0.4, and 0.5 C, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0006">6c</a>). The charge–discharge curves of Me-NVMP//HC at different rates are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0006">6d</a>, which display a pretty small polarization. The full cell could maintain a capacity of 112.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a retention of 80.39% after 200 cycles at 0.5 C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314019-fig-0006">6e</a>). These results indicate that the medium-entropy Me-NVMP cathode has excellent cycling stability and rate performance, which provides a solid foundation for future practical applications.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314019-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3e4e2edc-1299-41cc-be38-ce85c745f763/adfm202314019-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>

         </section>
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">

                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/9b06720a-0500-41d6-bbc1-320f6e0fc830/adfm202314019-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/aebcdc8c-5ce6-40d2-bee5-ae03a2baf951/adfm202314019-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9b06720a-0500-41d6-bbc1-320f6e0fc830/adfm202314019-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">

      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202314019-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202314019-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, a medium-entropy NASICON-type Na<sub>3.5</sub>V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> was rationally designed and successfully prepared as a sodium ion cathode. The structural degradation caused by Jahn-Teller distortion of MnO<sub>6</sub> and irreversible structural change above 4.0&nbsp;V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na is effectively depressed by regulating the configuration entropy in NASICON. Specifically speaking, the Me-NVMP can achieve an energy density of 550&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (1.8-4.4&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) at 0.1 C via the reversible redox reactions of V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup>/V<sup>5+</sup>, Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup>, Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup>, and Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup>. More impressively, after 10&nbsp;000 cycles at 100 C Me-NVMP cathode can still maintain a capacity retention of 83.5%. In addition, it also exhibits excellent cycling stability at low temperatures of 0 and −20 °C. The full cell assembled by the Me-NVMP cathode and hard carbon anode achieves a specific capacity of 162 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> based on the mass of the cathode. The intriguing strategy of regulation configuration entropy is believed to offer more insights for the development of new electrode materials.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

      <section class="article-section article-section__supporting" data-suppl="/doi/suppl/10.1002/adfm.202314019?onlyLog=true">
         <div class="accordion article-accordion">
